මූලෟ ප්‍රකාශය

ගිණුම පළබල සටහන්‌

01 ගිණුම්‌ පළිබඳ සටහන්‌

පොදුවේ පිළිගත්‌ ගිණුම මූලධර්ම වලට අනුකූලව රාජ්‍ය අංශයේ ගිණුමකරණ ප්‍රමිත කමිටුවේ අනුමත කරන
ලද ශිලංකා රාජ්‍ය අංශ ගිණුම්කරණ ප්‍රමිත තෝරා ගැනීම තුලින්‌ අවස්ථානෝචිත පරිද සාධාරණ ලෙස
ගිණුම්කරණ ඇස්තමේන්තු සකස්‌ කරමින්‌ මෙම ගිණුම්‌ ප්‍රකාශ ඉදිරිපත්‌ කර ඇත.

වංචා හෝ වැරදි හේතුවෙන්‌ ඇති විය හැකි ප්‍රමාණාත්මක සාවද්‍ය ප්‍රකාශයන්ගෙන්‌ තොරව මනා අභ්‍යන්තර
පාලනයක්‌ සැළසුම්‌ කිරීම සහ එය ක්‍රියාත්මක කිරීමට හා පවත්වාගෙන යාම තුළින්‌ සාධාරණ ලෙස මූල්‍ය
ප්‍රකාශන ඉදිරිපත්‌ කිරීමට කටයුතු කර ඇති බවට සහතික වෙමු.

02 ගිණුම්කරණ ප්‍රතිපත්ති

පිළිගත්‌ ගිණුම්කරණ ප්‍රතිපත්තීන්ට අනුකුලව අනන්‍ය වශයෙන්‌ කාලපරිච්ඡජේද පිළිබඳ අන්තර්සමබන්ධතාවයකින්‌
යුක්තව ළෙතිහාසික අය පදනම මත අධිකාරියේ ගිණුම්‌ වාර්තා ඉදිරිපත්‌ කර ඇත. මූල්‍ය ප්‍රතිපත්ති වලට
බලපෑ හැකි උද්ධමනකාරි සාධක අරභයා ගැලපුම්‌ කිරීමක්‌ කර නැති අතර උපචිත පදනම මත වාර්තා සකස්‌
කර ඇත.

038 අධිකාරයේ පිහිටීම

සහාධිපත්‍ය කළමනාකරණ අධිකාරිය , කොළඹ - 02 , ශ්‍රී චිත්තම්පලම ඒ ගාඩනර්‌ මාවත , ජාතික නිවාස
දෙපාර්තමේන්තු ගොඩනැගිල්ලේ පිහිටා ඇති අතර මුළු දවයිනටම අදාල වන පරිද සහාධිපත්‍ය දේපළ
සම්බන්ධ නියාමන කාර්යයන්‌ ඉටුකරනු ලබයි.

01 අධිකාරයේ නෛතික ස්වභාවය

2003 අංක 24 දරණ පොදු පහසුකම්‌ මණ්ඩල (සංශෝධන ) පනත මගින්‌ ලැබි ඇති බලතල අනුව සහාධිපත්‍ය
දේපලවල පොදු පහසුකම්‌ හා පොදු අංගෝපාංග නඩත්තුව , පරිපාලනය හා පාලනය සඳහා කළමනාකරණ
සංස්ථා පිහිටුවීම සහ ඒවා නියාමනය කිරීමත්‌ සහාධිපත්‍ය දේපළ ඉඳිකිරීමේදි එම දේපළවලට අදාල පොදු

1084.01.17 දනැතිව පළාත්පාලන නිවාස හා ඉදිකිරීම අමාත්‍යාංශය මගින්‌ යොමු කරන ලද අනුමැතියට අනුව
1084.01.10 දින රු.100ක කොටස්‌ 5000ක්‌ ශ්‍රී ලංකා නිවාස සංවර්ධන මූල්‍ය සංස්ථාවෙන්‌ ලබාගෙන ඇත.

එම කොටසක වටිනාකමට අදාලව 2000.06.29 දන කොටස්‌ 25,000ක ප්‍රසාද කොටස්‌ නිකුතුවක්‌ සිදූ කර ඇත.
මේ අනුව ග්‍රී ලංකා නිවාස සංවර්ධන මූල්‍ය සංස්ථාව නමින්‌ මෙම අධිකාරිය සතුව රු. 100 කොටස්‌ 30,000
සඳහා රු. 3,000,000ක ආයෝජනයක්‌ ගිණුම්වල හෙළිදරව්‌ කිරීමට කටයුතු කර ඇත.

18 රාජ්‍ය ප්‍රධාන ගිණුම්‌ නැබීම

2017 වර්ෂයේදිත්‌ භාණ්ඩාගාරය විසින්‌ දැනුවත්‌ කිරීම නගමු පුරවර ව්‍යාපෘතිය යටතේ සහාධිපත්‍ය දේපල
පාර්ශව දැනුවත්‌ කිරීමේ කටයුතු සඳහා රු. 10,000,000 ක්‌ වෙන්‌ කරන ලද අතර ඉන්‌ රැ 7,708,535 ක්‌
ප්‍රුවර්ථන වර්ෂයේදී වියදම්‌ කිරීමට කටයුතු කර ඇත. එමෙන්ම එම ව්‍යාපෘතිය සඳහා මිළ දී ගන්නා ලද
ස්ථාවර වත්කම්‌ වෙනුවෙන්‌ ක්ෂය වෙන්‌ කිරීම්‌ සඳහා රු 119,081 ක මුදලක්ද ප්‍රවරථන වර්ෂයේදී ව්‍යාපෘති
වියදම්වලට ඇතුලත්‌ කිරීමට කටයුතු කර ඇත.

මූල්‍ය ප්‍රකාශය

මහියංගන සතිපොළ

ආර්‌ බාලසිංහම්‌

ප්‍රයිම හෝම්ස්‌

බලූ මවුන්ටන්ට රෙසිඩන්සීස්‌
සීකොෝ සඩසිවලොජප්මන්ට

හිරු සිවලොජ්මන්ට

හෝම ලැන්ඩස්‌

සම්ලන්ක්‌ සිවලොජප්මන්ට
එම. අබේසූරිය

කේ ආර්‌ බුදටස්‌

කළා.
බොල්‌ හා අඩමාන ණය වෙන්‌ කිරීම

කාර්්‍යය මණ්ඩල ණය සහ අත්තිකාරම්‌
ස්වාභාවික ආපදා ණය

විශේෂ අත්තිකාරම්‌

ආපලා ණය

විශේෂ ආපදා ණය

උත්සව අත්තිකාරම්‌

පොත්‌ මිලදී ගැනීම්‌ අත්තිකාරම්‌

ගමන්‌ වියදම්‌ අත්තිකාරම්‌

මිලදී ගැනීම්‌ අත්තිකාරම්‌

oostoyekaljeyioknleyokeiiol kee olslohlele)

ලංකා විදුලි බල මණ්ඩලය

නගමු පුරවර                          උපලේඛණ 15
අනවසර ඉදිකිරීම ඉවත්කීරීම - ජා.නි.ස.අ

lone)

එකතු කල අගය මත බදු

ජාතිය ගොඩනැගීමේ බදු

විවිධ අත්තිකාරම්‌

එඩිමන්ටන්‌ රජයේ සේවක නිවාස ක්‍රමයේ නිදන්ගත අරමුදල්‌
සර්පන්ටයින්‌ රජයේ නිවාස ක්‍රමයේ නඩත්තු අරමුදල
ස්වයංසවිය "සොයිසාපුර නිවාස ක්‍රමය"

1.9 විගණනයේ වගකීම

මාගේ විගණනය මත පදනමට මෙම මූල්‍ය
ප්‍රකාශන පිළිබදව මතයක්‌ ප්‍රකාශ කිරීහම
මාගේ වගකීම වේ. මා විසින්‌ උත්තරීතර
විගණන ආයනයන්ගේ ජාත්‍යන්තර
විගණන පුමිතිවලට (ISSAI 1000-1810)
අනුරුප ශී ලංකා විගණන පුමිතිවලට
අනුකූලව මාගේ විගණනය සිදු කරන

විටත්‌ එම්‌ කාර්යය සිදූ කර නොතිබූ අතර 2018 ප්‍රසම්පාදන සැලැස්මටද ඇතුළත්‌ කර
තිබුණ.

2014 පෙබරවාරි 17 දිනැති අංක 01/2014 දරන රාජ්‍ය මුදල්‌ චක්‍රලේඛයේ 3.2 ඡේදය
ප්‍රකාරව ක්‍රියාකාරී සැලැස්මෙගි වාර්ෂික ප්‍රසම්පාදන සැලැස්ම ඇතුළත්‌ චී නොනිබුණි.

අයවැය පාලනය

අධිකාරිය විසින්‌ ඉදිරිපත්‌ කරන ලද මූල්‍ය ප්‍රකාශන අනුව අයවැයගත හා තථ්‍ය සංඛ්‍යා අතර
සියයට 20 සිට සියයට 307 දක්වා චිචවලනයන්‌ නිරික්ෂණය වූ බැවින්‌ අයවැය ලේඛනය ඵලදායී

කළමනාකරණ පාලන කාරකයක්‌ ලෙස භාචිතා කර නොතිබුණි.

වාර්ෂික වාර්තා සභාගත කිරීම

අයිකාරිය විසින්‌ 2015 සහ 2016 වර්ෂයන්ට අදාල වාර්ෂික වාර්තා 2018 ජූලි වන විටත්‌
පාර්ලිමේන්තුවේ සභාගත කර නොතිබුණි.

1.     පද්ධති භා පාලනයන්‌

විගණනයේදී නිරික්ෂණය වූ පද්ධනි හා පාලන අඩුපාඩු වරින්‌ චර අයිකාරියේ සභාපතිවරයාගේ
අවධානයට යොමු කරන ලදී. පහත සඳහන්‌ පාලන ක්ෂේත්‍ර කෙරෙහි විශේෂ අවධානය යොමුකළ

යුතුවේ.

(ආ සහාධිපත්‍ය ලළේපල                   - කළමනාකරණ සංස්ථා අධීක්ෂණය විධිමන්‌ නොවීම.
කළමනාකරණය                 ~ සහායිපත්‍ය දේපලවල පොදූ පහසුකම්‌ පැවරීමේ

- අනවසර ඉදිකිරීම්‌ සම්බන්ධ වාර්තා පවත්වා
නොතිබීම.

- කලින්‌ ලබාගන්‌ අත්තිකාරම්‌ පියවීමට පෙර නැවත එම
නිලධාරීන්ට අත්තිකාරම්‌ නිකුන්‌ කිරීම
- මාණ්ඩලික නොවන නිලධාරීන්ට අත්තිකාරම්‌ නිකුත්‌

Dhjectives ofthe
nuthorily

I Me ee

Control, manage, maintain and administer the
Condominium parcels, the Common elements
and the common amenities of the Condominium
Property or Semi Condominium Property;

Ensure the common elements and the Common
Amenities of the Condominium Property or Semi
Condominium Property are properly maintained
in good order and that periodic repairs are being
Carried out in order to maintain such property
in good and serviceable order, and to assist the
management corporation or the owner or owners
or occupiers to Carry out such activities in the event
of the management corporation or owner or owners
or occupiers failing to carry out such activities;

Ensure that all buildings comprising such
Condominium parcels are insured against risk of fire,
civil commotion and riot or to insure or keep insured,
if so requested by the management corporation
or by the owners, and to recover such premium or
Charges from the management corporation or the
owners as the case may be;

Remove all such unauthorized constructions erected
or carried out by the respective owners or occupiers
of such Condominium Parcels or by any person,
Contrary to the registered Condominium Plan of
the Condominium Property or the registered Semi
Condominium Property;

Ensure that the management corporation of the
Condominium Property or Semi Condominium
Property are properly functioning and to manage
and administer the activities of such management
Corporation;

Assist the management corporation or the owner or
owners or occupiers of the Condominium Parcels, of
the Condominium Property or Semi Condominium
Property in providing the services such as water,
Sewerage, drainage, gas, electricity, garbage disposal,
air conditioning, telephone, radio and redifussion
Services to the owner or owners or occupiers of
the Condominium Parcels of such Condominium
Property or Semi Condominium Property;

Assist the management corporation to establish
and maintain for use by owners or occupiers of
Such condominium parcels , facilities such as roads
, access ways , lawns , gardens , parks , play grounds
and other open spaces , or to be directly involved
with such activities in the event of the management
Corporation failing to establish and maintain such
facilities

Transfer to the local authority the maintenance
of roads, access ways, lawns, gardens, parks,
playgrounds, and other open spaces for the use by
owners or occupiers of the Condominium Parcels of
the Condominium Property or Semi Condominium
Property;

Provide maintenance and repair services to such
Condominium Parcels of the Condominium Property
or Semi Condominium property at the request of
the management corporation or owners or occupiers
thereof;

Monitor the progress of the construction of the
registered provisional Condominium Property in
order to ensure that the interests of the stakeholders
are protected and to intervene wherever necessary
to protect such interests;

Formulate and submit Condominium re-
development program including capital investment
plans to the Minister for approval by the Government

Li

Call upon the National Housing Development
Authority or the Urban Development Authority
or any local authority or any government agency
or any private sector developer, to undertake
the implementation of such Condominium re-
development projects, or to undertake the
execution of the Condominium re-development
projects, of such program as may be approved by
the Government;

Undertake the completion of any Condominium
Building shown in the registered Semi Condominium
Plan or Provisional Condominium Plan , in the event
of any owner failing to complete such project,

Develop or re-develop land for carrying out of any of
the objectives of the Authority and

Do all such other acts as may be necessary or
conducive to the attainment of any or all of the
above objectives.

Report of the Administrative

In the year 2017, an income of Rs. 258.1 million was
generated through the operational activities of the
Authority. In Comparison to operational income in the
year 2016 which amounted to Rs. 107.254 million, the
operational income has posted a growth of 30.85%.
The overall expenditure in the year 2016 was Rs. 109.44
million and in comparison, the overall expenditure in 2017
was Rs. 140.56 million. The net post tax profitin year 2017
was Rs 98.82 million and significantly, this was the highest
profit recorded during the period from year 2003 to date.

This increase in the income can be attributable to the
following factors prevailed in the condominium property
sector.

> Notable increase in the construction of new
Condominium properties

> Increase in the construction of condominium
properties by both the state and private sectors
from year 2015.

> Arrival of foreign investors for the construction
of large scale mix condominium properties in
Colombo City.

> The decision to levy 25% of the value of the
certificate in issuing initial planning condominium
Clearance certificate from year 2016. .

Issuance of initial clearance
for the construction of
condominium properties

Prior to the submission of a building application for the
Construction of a condominium property, a clearance
letter is issued by the Authority in respect of the
Condominium property proposed to be constructed,
having inspected the proposed land on which the property
to be Constructed. Accordingly, initial clearance was
granted to 205 Condominium properties proposed to be
Constructed in 2016 and 198 clearance letters were issued
in 2017. These clearance instructions served as guidance
to property developers in the construction activities.

Issuance of Condominium
Certificates

Having inspected whether the common elements and
Common amenities are properly and adequately available
in the condominium properties constructed by the public
or private sectors, the Condominium Management
Authority, which is the regulatory body established under
the Common Amenities Board (Amendment) Act No. 24
of 2003 issues a condominium certificate. In issuing this
certificate, the Authority acts in compliance with the
provisions of the Apartment Ownership Act No.11 of 1973
and it paves the way for the unit owners of the property
to have undisturbed possession of the common amenities
and common elements.

Further, the income generated through the issuance of
Condominium certificates is the main source of income of
the Authority. From 2005 up to 31.12.2017, the Authority
has issued 1151 such certificates. It was planned to issue
210 certificates in the year 2017 and the Authority was
able to issue 154 certificates by the end of the year.

Accordingly, details of certificates issued by the
Authority during the period from 2014 to 2016 are
tabulated below.

Annual        Progress
targets

2015

2017
Physical                210              154

Of the applications forwarded in the year 2017 seeking
to obtain condominium certificates, certificates were not
issued in respect of 14 of them owing to the non —issue of
certificate of compliance, and other shortcomings.

Anew trend inthe construction of condominium property
has emerged with then entry of foreign investors into the
Condominium sector in 2014.

An increasing trend in the construction of properties is
witnessed also due to the construction of condominium
properties by the Urban Development Authority for
resettling tenement settlers and the construction of
500,000 houses under the new programme of the
government.

Nearly 57 buildings constructed by the private sector
are unable to apply for the certification of the Authority
on account of being unable to obtain certificates of
Compliance. There are 85 such properties of the National
Housing Development Authority aswell. Inordertoaddress
this issue, the Authority as the regulator of the sector, has
initiated measures to amend the Apartment Ownership
Act No 04 of 1009 and the relevant amendments were
approved by Parliament on 08.08.2013.

As per Apartment Ownership Act No 11 of 1973, it is not
mandatory to register a condominium plan. Therefore,
new amendments have been proposed making it
mandatory for the registration of all condominium plans
and a report to that effect has been referred to the Legal
Draftsman for necessary action.

Establishing, registering
and actively maintaining
Management Corporations

Though a property with private ownership is maintained by
the owners of such property, the maintenance of common

10


Report of the Administrative

elements and Common amenities in a condominium
property with shared ownership cannot be maintained
by any single individual and as such all those who share
these Common elements and common amenities band
together to constitute management corporations which
are the legal structure for their administration.

From the year 2005 up to now, the authority has
constituted (management corporations in 930
Condominium properties.

The progress achieved in establishing Management
Corporations by the Authority from 2015 up to 2017 is
Summarized in the following table.

However, the following difficulties were experienced in
establishing management corporations

mn Lack of understanding among property owners
regarding the importance of the Management
Corporation for maintaining property

mn Lack of interest among residents of the apartment
housing schemes constructed by the government
agencies such as the Urban Development
Authority for the establishment of management
Corporations

mn Owners of condominium property constructed
by the private sector not residing permanently in
them

mn 1assitude of owners tobe involvedinmaintenance
and management activities under a voluntary
basis due to them being busy.

mn Defaulting the payment of maintenance fees and
other residents not cooperating with the panel of
office bearers of the Management Corporation.

mn Objectionsraisedbythemajorityofoccupantsover
the high prevalence of unauthorized structures
in condominium properties constructed by the
government.

Resolving disputes of
Condominium Property

The Authority has been vested with powers Common
Amenities Board Law No 10 of 1073 to intervene in the
event of disputes arising between the management of
the condominium property and the property owner or
between the residents and the owner or between the
owner and the buyer. Accordingly, when a complaint is
forwarded to the Authority in writing by those who have
entered into a sales agreement to purchase condominium
property or a resident, the Authority initiates necessary
action for its prompt resolution. Dispute which cannot be
resolved are referred to an investigation.

An investigation council has been set up for the resolution
of such disputes. The complaints received by the Council
Can be categorized as follows according to their nature.

e Not granting deeds to the residents since the
Condominium Plan cannot be registered despite
the lapse of a long period of time since the
Construction and sale through a sales agreement.

mn Construction inviolation of the approved building
plan; some property developers are unable to
obtain the certificate of compliance as they have
executed sales agreement after constructing only
Several floors.

mn Not providing common amenities and common
elements in accordance with the approved plan

mn Residents not paying the monthly maintenance
fee to the Management Corporation

mn Erecting unauthorized structures and problems
arising in using car parks and the public areas

In the year 2016, the Authority has taken measures to
resolve 65 complaints so received.

No of disputes resolved
2015                                  60
2016                                  65
2017                                  82

Institutional mechanism to
respond positively to public
arievances

> Uponreceiving a complaint, forwarding a copy of
the complaint within 03 days to the respondent
party and obtaining observations within 14 days.

> Summoning the complainant and the respondent
for an inquiry within a week of receiving
observations

11


Report of the Administrative

> If there is a solution, reporting it on the first day
itself and concluding the inquiry

> Recording verbal or written evidence

e Giving an order within 03 months of initiating the
inquiry

Awareness Programmes

Educating Management Corporations, which is the legal
structure of residents of Condominium property as
provided for by the Apartment Ownership Act No. 11 of
1973 and the Common Amenities Board Law No. 10 of
1973 and creating awareness among property developers
and other stakeholders on the administration and
maintenance of the property has to be carried out on a
regular basis.

Accordingly, the following measures were implemented
under a Rs. 10.0 million treasury provision in the year
2017 to creating awareness among all stakeholders of the
Condominium property.

> Creating awareness amongst residents of

Condominium properties.

> Educating public sector officials involved in the
sector.

> Awareness programmes for police officers of the
Western Province.

> Distribution of ‘Condominium’ journal containing
educational materials on condominium properties
and leaflets to create awareness on condominium
life style.

Transferring Ownership of
Tsunami property constructed
under Tsunami rehabilitation

The following facts transpired during the survey conducted
by the Authority on condominium property constructed
under Tsunami rehabilitation.

e The number of housing schemes constructed
as flats is 39 and the number of housing units is
3749.

e The number of houses schemes constructed
as twin houses (joint) is 30 and the number of
housing units is 2064.

The Authority, having taken into account the fact that no
measures had been taken to dispose of the ownership
of these housing schemes, took this matter up with the
Ministry of Land and Land Development which owns
these lands and as a result such negotiations the approval
of the Cabinet of Ministers was secured to introduce
amendments to the Land Act to enable the transfer of

ownership of such lands and the drafting of relevant
regulations has been finalized by now and action has
been initiated to refer same to the Legal Draftsman'’s
Department.

For this purpose, the Authority conducted 02 workshops
in partnership with the Ministry of Land, the Land
Department and the Survey Department and the draft
of the necessary regulations was formulated. Action

is also being pursued in collaboration with the District
Secretary, Matara to award deeds in respect of two
apartment housing schemes in the Matara district.

Regulatory interventions of
Condominium Management
Authority

Employing the aforementioned powers and provisions,
the Condominium Management Authority has been able
to execute the following very important services during
the year 2017.

> Measures were initiated in the year 2015 to
seek the approval of the Cabinet to amend
the Apartment Ownership (Special Provisions)
Act No 04 of 1994 enabling the registration of
properties which had been constructed several
decades ago but which have not been registered
as a Condominium property thus preventing the
handing over of their ownership to the residents
and this process was expedited in the year 2017
which led to the passage of the Act on 08.08.2018
and it will bring benefits to 8000 families who
have not been able to obtain deeds for nearly 15
years.

> The panel of experts appointed by the Cabinet of
Ministers to make amendments to the Common
Amenities Law No. 10 of 1973 and Apartment
Ownership Act No. 11 of 1073 has by now
Suggested all the necessary amendments and
Same was referred to the Legal Draftsman. The
amended bill will address most of the practical
issues in the condominium sector and enable the
Authority to offer a wider range of services.

Regulations made under the Condominium Management
Authority Law and the Apartment Ownership Act
were published in Gazette Extraordinary No 2026/25
dated 05 July 2017. It should be noted that this gazette
notification could only be issued nearly 10 years after the
establishment of this Authority.

Meetings of the Board of
Directors and Meetings of Audit
and Management Committees

In the year 2017, 06 Board meetings were held and
decisions were taken as regards a host of important board
papers associated with the sector. 03 meetings of Audit
and Management Committee were held.

1.2 Management's Responsibility for the Financial Statements

Management is responsible for
preparation and fair presentation
of these financial statements in
accordance with Sri Lanka Accounting
Standards.    This    responsibility
includes: designing, implementing and
maintaining internal controls relevant
tothe preparationandfair presentation
of financial statements that are free
from material misstatements.

1.3 Auditor's Responsibility

My responsibility is to express an
opinion on these financial statements
based on my audit. | conducted my
audit in accordance with Sri Lanka
auditing Standards corresponding
to international audit standards of
supreme audit institutions. (ISSA
1000-1810) Those standards require
that we plan and perform the audit to
obtain reasonable assurance whether
the financial statements are free from
material misstatements.

An audit involves performing
procedures to obtain audit evidence
about the amounts and disclosures
in the financial statements. The
procedures selected depend on the
auditor's judgment, including the
assessment of the risk of the material
misstatement of the consolidated
financial statements, whether due to
fraud or error. In making those risk
assessments, the auditor Considers
internal Control relevant to the
Authority's preparation and fair
presentation of the Consolidated
financial statements in order to
design audit procedures that
appropriate in the circumstances,
but not for the purpose of expressing
an opinion on the effectiveness of
the Authority's internal control.
An audit also includes evaluating
the appropriateness of Accounting
Policies used and the reasonableness
of accounting estimates made by
management, as well as evaluating the
overall presentation of the financial
Statements.

11 Basis for the Qualified Audit Opinion

qualify my opinion on the basis of
matters referred to in paragraph 2.2 of

suspending Lanka Net Company from paying Rs.
807,187 payable to the CMA and the legal interest
thereon of Rs 2,482,77a/-out of the money to be
received by Lanka Net from the Department of

payable by the Department of Buildings in the
Case No. 222/2001, the two parties have not yet
reached an agreement over the amount to be
paid. Once the two parties reach an agreement
over the payment , Lanka Net has given an
undertaking at the Commercial high Court to
settle the amount due to the CMA. Accordingly,
the case No. 222/2001 is due to be taken up for
hearing again on 26.11.2018 for the consideration
of the agreement and case No. DMR 53429 is to
be called again on 15.03.2019 to progress of that
Case.

Thus, it would be possible to have this amount
settled by recovering the amount due from Lanka
Net brought forward for 18 years together with
the interest thereon.

1. Onerating Review

Performance
1i.1. Functioning and review
(a)   The progress in respect of   It has been mentioned in the audit report that | Agreed with the
the registration of management   the targets in respect of the registration and answer of the

Corporations and committees and
renewal/ reactivation of registration of
dormant committees was around 45%
and the achievement of the targeted
objectives pertaining to Tsunami
Condominium properties was at a very
low level. The following observations
are made in this regard.

(1)    Even though the Authority
had conducted 101 awareness
programmes for beneficiaries in the
year under review for the attainment
of the objectives of the Authority
spending a sum of Rs. 8.102 million,
only 46 management Corporations
had been registered. Accordingly, the
progress achieved was only 45 percent.

renewal) reactivation of registration of Tsunami
management corporations could not be achieved.

However, the practical circumstances that
Caused such a situation are outlined below for
your information. In terms of the Apartment
Ownership Act No 11 of 1073 as amended by
Act No. 3°9o0f 2003 and Act No. 45 of 1982, with
the registration of a Condominium plan of a
Condominium property at the land registry, its
lawful management corporation is established.
The Control, maintenance, management and
administration of common amenities and common
elements in such a condominium property should
be Carried out by its management corporation.
But in 95% of Tsunami condominium properties,
the deeds had not been granted by registering the
Condominium plan. Therefore the management
Corporations cannot be established.

As per the above explanations and the provisions of
the Act, though these condominium properties are
not subject to the regulation of the Authority, for
the benefits of residents “covering management
Committees” were established o their request
for the control, maintenance, management and
administration of common amenities and common
elements.

Authority

At present, these condominium properties
are administered by the respective Divisional
Secretariats and as a result of hitherto not granting
deeds, the residents have not shown any interest
in updating the management committees.

Owing to the reasons outlined above, estimated
figures in respect of the reestablishment of
Tsunami management corporations or renewal of
registration could not be achieved successfully.

21



Audit Report

Lelio

Answer of the Authority

Recommenda-
lel e) Ai TTeli
Erle Fults

committee

Taking stock of this situation and also having
regard for the need for properly carrying out
maintenance activities by activating management
Corporations by granting deeds for these houses
without the Certificate of conformity, the
Apartment Ownership (Special Provisions) Act
was passed by Parliament on 08 August 2018.
With the enforcement of the new Act, it will be
possible to establish management corporations
after the granting of deeds for these houses by
the relevant public sector institutions. Accordingly,
132 management corporations are proposed tobe
established.

Accordingly, 132 management corporations are
proposed to be established.

(i)   Even though plans had been
made to earn Rs. 245,000, Rs 1,120,000
and Rs 350,000 during the year
under review from the registration
of management corporations and
committees and reactivating the
registration of public, private and
Tsunami condominium properties, no
income could be earned in respect
of the establishment of management
Corporations in Tsunami condominium
properties and the income from the
public sector too was only Rs. 95,8683.

(bh)    Even though the Authority had

at the end of the year.

Even though, it was estimated to study 320

Complaints, only 99 complaints had been received

Complaints remains to be resolved is 17. Inquiries
regarding the Complaints thus remained to be
resolved are inquiries commenced during the tail
end of the year. They have been resolved by mid-
2018. Therefore there has not a delay.

Agreed with the
answer of the
Authority

(Cc)    Since the amendments to
Common Amenities Board Act No 10
of 1073 and Apartment Ownership Act

to be finalized in year 2015 had not
been completed in the relevant year
and even though the time had been
extended up to year 2017, even by the

Acts had only been furnished to the
Legal Draftsman’s Department.

As per a decision of the cabinet of ministers in year
2016, it was decided to appoint a panel of experts
for the process of furnishing relevant amendments
to the Common Amenities Board (Amendment) Act
No.10 of 1973. All draft amendments formulated
by the said panel having met on a number of
occasions in year 2017 were furnished to the

request was also made to the Secretary of the
Ministry of Justice by letter dated 29.11.2017 to
have the amended draft prepared expeditiously.
(AnnexNos. 10, 10(1)). The relevant activities are
now being carried out by the Legal Draftsman’s
Department.

structures.

2.       Residents jointly staging vehement protest
Campaigns when action is taken for the removal of
unauthorized constructions.

3.   Various other difficulties encountered in
removing unauthorized structures.

Authority to recover the expenditure incurred in
removing unauthorized constructions, the relevant
parties had failed to make the payments.

proceedings, such a course of action would be
uneconomical and therefore no particular interest
had been shown in that regard.

Ll Underutilization of funds

Capital grants received annually for
the capital projects Carried out by the
Authority are shown under current
liabilities in the financial statements
without being utilized for the relevant
purposes and that sum amounted
to Rs. 25,421,000 in the year 2017
and Rs. 42,209,311 in the year 2016.
The Chairman had reported to be on
20 August 2018, that the provisions
remained unspent as the contractor
did not carry out the relevant activities
and that account would be taken to
release the savings to the Ministry.

The Treasury has granted Rs 10 million for the
disposal of ownership of residents relevant to the
Tsunami condominium properties and as problems
have encountered by Divisional Secretaries as
regard the transfer of lands of such housing
schemes, the activities pertaining to the transfer
of lands have been crippled.

In view of this situation, certificates of conformity
Could not be obtained for the relevant properties
and therefore the ownership disposal activities
have been delayed. Accordingly, action has been
taken to carry forward a sum of Rs. 6,385, 670/=
out of the provisions allocated in the accounts.

Similarly, a sum of Rs. 143.2 million was received in
the year 2015 for the renovation of internal roads
and drain systems of government housing schemes
and the contract for the renovation was awarded
to the State Development and Construction
Corporation under a cabinet decision.

However, as a result of Contractor not carrying
out some of the planned activities, a sum of Rs
19, 035,330/- was saved and action was taken to
Carry forward it under current liabilities.

This matter will be examined further and action
will be taken to release remaining amount to the
Ministry of Housing and Construction.

Agreed with the
answer of the
Authority

committee

(a)     Even though approval had been
granted for two posts of Assistant
General Manager for the legal affairs
according to the approved Cadre,
organizational structure and scheme
of recruitment of the Authority , a
permanent officer had been recruited
only for one post. The service of
another Legal Officer also obtained on
the daily payment basis from the year
2008 and a payment of Rs.554,000
had been made in the year 2017 for
the duties of that Legal Officer on the
approval of the Board of Directors. The
Chairman had reported that though
the services of an experienced lawyer
was required to handle the work in
this sector, such a lawyer could not be
recruited due to the salary structure
of the Authority and therefore the
services of a lawyer had been obtained
on temporary basis.

There are two posts of Assistant General Manager
for the Legal Division and a permanent officer
has been recruited for one post. For the other
post, officers have been appointed on part-time
basis. As the Legal Division handles the cases of
the Authority in respect of condominium law, the
Services of an expert lawyer well experienced in
this sector is required for this purpose than of an
ordinary lawyer.

When applications were called for the post through
notices in public newspapers, the post could not
be filled as such applicants could not be found
and such a lawyer cannot be recruited within the
Salary structure applicable to an Assistant General
Manager of the Authority.

Therefore the services of a lawyer with more than
30 years of experience at the National Housing
Development Authority and the National Housing
Commissioner's Office are procured three days
per week with an allowance of Rs 3000 per day
with the approval of the Board of Directors. Here
the maximum expenditure per month would
approximately be Rs. 36,000/=. This is less than
half the amount of the expenditure to be incurred
if a fulltime officer was appointed.

At a discussion held regarding the procurement
of services of an external lawyer, the Department
of Management Services informed that the
matter should be submitted for the approval of
the Department of Management Services of the
Treasury and action will be taken accordingly.

6.2 Budgetary Control

According to the financial statements
presented by the Authority, actual
income and expenditure revealed
variances ranging from 26 per cent to
307 per cent, thus indicating that the
budget had not been made use of as
an effective instrument of financial
management control.

The Authority has taken action to minimize actual
expenditure than budgeted values by controlling
other expenses other than the statutory expenses
and the increase of office rental by the National
Housing Development Authority and the increase
in the insurance premium pertaining to new
recruitments too have contributed to this situation.

In the absence of projects carried out using
budgetary provisions in the year 2017, the
Service Charge income has taken a lower value
and though the certificate income was estimated
taking into account Condominium properties
being constructed in the country,, due to the non-
Completion of them within the year resulted in the
income of the current year being lower than the
estimated income.

Similarly, the registration fees, Condominium
publication income, administrative fees and
tender income were below the estimated value
and the non-registration of contractors too had a
significant impact.

These circumstances also had an impact on the
tender income. However plans have been made
to use the budget as an effective instrument of
financial management control in the year 20183.

The committee
Gave instructions
to     prepare
estimates taking
into    account
practical
Situations,   to
amend     the
budget     for
updating   that
document   by
taking     into
consideration
actual income
and expenditure
at the end of
the year and

to      maintain
the budget as
an      efrective

instrument    of
control.

6.3 Tabling of Annual Reports

The Authority had not tabled the
Annual Reports relevant to the years
2015 and 2016 in parliament even by
July 2013.

The Annual Reports relevant to the years 2015
and 2016 have been furnished to the Ministry of
Housing and Construction to be submitted to the
Cabinet of Ministers.

The Chairman,

Condominium Management Authority

Rcport of the Auditor General on the Financial Statements of the Condominium
Management Authority for the year ended 31 December 2016 in terms of Section 14(2)(0)
of the Finance Act No. 33 of 1071.

The audit of financial statements of the Condominium Management Authority for the year ended
31 December 2016 comprising the statement of financial position as at 31 December 2016 and
the statement of financial performance, statement of changes in equity and cash flow statement
for the year then ended and a summary of significant accounting policies and other explanatory
information, was carried out under my direction in pursuance of provisions in Article 154(1) of
the Constitution of the Democratic Socialist Republic of Sri Lanka read in conjunction with
Section 13(1) of the Finance Act, No.3$8 of 1071 and Section 21 of the Common Amenities
Board Law, No.10 of 1973. My comments and observations which I consider should be
published with the Annual Report of the Authority in terms of Section 14(2)(c) of the Finance
Act appear in this report.

1.2 Management’s Responsibility for the Financial Statements

Management is responsible for the preparation and fair presentation of these financial
statements in accordance with Sri Lanka Public Sector Accounting Standards and for
such internal control as the management determines is necessary to enable the preparation
of financial statements that are free from material misstatements whether due to fraud or

Crror.

1.3 Auditor’s Responsibility

My responsibility is to express an opinion on these financial statements based on my
audit. I conducted my audit in accordance with Sri Lanka Auditing Standards consistent

with International Auditing Standards of Supreme Audit Institutions (ISSAT 1000 —


[=

AGDSL

විගච/ධිපන ලැප නල නඩ)
ටගනකාධටරත මඳපාටතම නනවට

bonibuiiinitalt bent iii beomii bs

Auditor General's Department

1810). Those Standards require that 1 comply with ethical requiremenis and plan and
perform the audit to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the financial statements

are free from material misstatements.

An audit involves performing procedures to obtain audit evidence about the amounts and
disclosures in the financial statements. The procedures selected depend on the auditor's
judgement, including the assessment of the risks of material misstatement of the financial
statements, whether due to fraud or error. In making those risk assessments, the auditor
considers internal control relevant to the Authority’s preparation and fair presentation of
the financial statements in order to design audit procedures that are appropriate in the
circumstances, but not for the purpose of expressing an opinion on the effectiveness of
the Authority’s internal control. An audit also includes evaluating the appropriateness of
accounting policies. used and the reasonableness  of accounting estimates made by
management, as well as evaluating the overall presentation of financial statements. Sub-
sections (3) and (4) of Section 13 of the Finance Act, No.33 of 1071 give discretionary

powers to the Auditor General to determine the scope and extent of the audit.

I believe that the audit evidence I have obtained is sufficient an appropriate to provide a

basis for my audit opinion.

14 Basis for Qualified Opinion

My opinion is qualified based on the matters described in paragraph 2.2 of this report.

2,        Financial Statements

2.1 Qualified Opinion

In my opinion, except for the effects of the matters described in paragraph 2.2 of this
report the financial statements give a true and fair view of the financial position of the
Condominium Management Authority as at 31 December 2016 and its financial
performance and cash flow for the year then ended in accordance with Sri Lanka Public

Sector Accounting Standards.

              2.2      Comments on Financial Statements

2.2.1 Srilanka Public Sector Accounting Standards

The following observations are made.

(a) Sri Lanka Public Sector Accounting Standard 02

Adjustments made in the statement of changes in equity for the gratuity and
depreciations relating to the year 2015 amounting to Rs.650,410 and Rs.187,007
respectively had been adjusted to the cash flow for the operating activities in the cash
flow statement in the year under review .Nevertheless, the prior year adjustments
totalling Rs.1,130,822 made in the year under review had been adjusted to the cash

flow on the financial activities of the year under review.

(b) Sri Lanka Public Sector Accounting Standard 07

As useful life time of an asset should be reviewed considering as a change of the

accounting estimate at the date of the end of the period reported in cach year.

Nevertheless, the Authority had not taken action in respect of the assets totalling
Rs.20.80 million had been fully depreciated but are being further used.

(©) Sri Lanka Public Sector Accounting Standard 00

Even though, the final stock shall be computed and accounted at the lower value of
cost or net realizable value, contrary to that the Authority had valued the stock on
the cost without being computed at the net realizable valuc by making policy for the

Stock .

2.2.2 Accounting Deficiencies

The following accounting deficiencies were observed.

(4 As the office rent which payments were completed in the year 2016 had been re-
allocated, the Office Rent Account and the Accrued Office Rent Account had
been over computed by Rs.115,802.

(by) Action had not been taken to pay or bring to account during the year under review
under current liabilities the gratuity amounting to Rs.315,418 which had been

Financial Review

Financial Results

According to the financial statements presented, the surplus of the Authority for the year
ended 31 December 2010 amounted to Rs.70.41 million as compared with the
corresponding surplus of Rs.21.97 million for the preceding year, thus indicating an
improvement of Rs.48.44 million in the financial results for the year under review as
compared with the preceding year. Even though receipt of Treasury provisions for the
payment of salaries had decreased by Rs.11 million as compared the year under review
with the preceding year, the increase of the operating income by a sum of Rs.76.8

million had been the main reason for the above improvement.

An analysis of the financial results of the year under review and the 04 preceding years
revealed that, despite the deficits incurred in the year 2013, surpluses had been earned in
other years . Even though the contribution of the Authority, after the adjustment of
employees’ remuneration, the taxes paid to the Government and the adjustment of
depreciation of non-current assets, had improved from the year 2012 to the year 2016, the
improvement in the year under review, as compared with the preceding year , was 53 per

Cent.

Analytical Financial Review

The following observations are made.

(4) Due tothe income from the issue of certificates for the condominium properties
had increased by Rs.83.60 million or 107 per cent as compared with the preceding
year, the operating income of the year under review had been increased by
Rs.76.8 million or 72 per cent . As such, due to increase of the interest income for
fixed assets the non-operating income had been increased by Rs.6.16 million or

120 per cent as compared with the preceding year.

3.       Financial Review

3.1      Financial Results

According to the financial statements presented, the surplus of the Authority for thc year
ended 31 December 2016 amounted to Rs.70.41 million as compared with the
corresponding surplus of Rs.21.97 million for the preceding year, thus indicating an
improvement of Rs.48.44 million in the financial results for the year under review as
compared with the preceding year. Even though receipt of Treasury provisions for the
payment of salaries had decreased by Rs.11 million as compared the year under review
with the preceding year, the increase of the operating income by a sum of Rs.76.8

million had been the main reason for the above improvement.

An analysis of the financial results of the year under review and the 04 preceding years
revealed that, despite the deficits incurred in the year 2013, surpluses had been earned in
other years . Even though the contribution of the Authority, after the adjustment of
employees’ remuneration, the taxes paid to the Government and the adjustment of
depreciation of non-current assets, had improved from the year 2012 to the year 2016, the
improvement in the year under review, as compared with the preceding year , was 53 per

Cent.

3.2 Analytical Financial Review

6                   The following observations arc made.

(4) Due to the income from the issue of certificates for the condominium properties
had increased by Rs.83.60 million or 107 per cent as compared with the preceding
year, the operating income of the year under review had been increased by
Rs.76.8 million or 72 per cent . As such, due to increase of the interest income for
fixed assets the non-operating income had been increased by Rs.6.16 million or

120 per cent as compared with the preceding year.

4.5       Identified Losses

The Authority had not included the Cost of Living Allowance in the calculation of the
Employce Provident Fund and Employee Trust Fund for the period from January 2000 to
December 2013 contrary to Section 47 of the Employee Provident Fund Act.No.l5 of
1058. As such, action had not been taken to recovery of the sum of Rs.4.47 milion which
was the employee share included in the outstanding Employee Provident Fund
amounting to Rs.11.18 million paid by the Authority from the relevant persons . Further
the Authority had to pay a surcharge of Rs.6.36 million for that outstanding money and a
sum of Rs.2.94 million had been paid for that purpose in the year 2010.

5.       Accountability and Good Governance

5.1     Action Plan

The following observations are made

(a) Annual Procurement Plan, Human Resources Development Plan and Internal
Audit Plan should be included in the Action Plan in terms of the Paragraph 5-2 of
the Public Finance Circular No.01/2014 dated 17 February 2014. However, those

had not been included init.

(         (bh Even though plans had been made to complete the amendments of the
Condominium Property Management Authority Act, No.10 of 1073 in August
2015 , according to the Action Plan of the year 2016 that period had been
extended up to February 2016. However, that activities had not been completed
by the end of the year under review and the relevant Act had been referred to the

Department of Legal Draftsman.

5.2 Budgetary Control

According to the financial statements presented by the Authority, actual income and
expenditure revealed variances ranging from 15 per cent to 87 per cent, thus indicating
that the budget had not been made use of as an effective instrument of financial

0                    management control.

5.3 Tabling of Annual Reports

The Authority had not tabled the Annual Reports relevant to the years 2013,2014 and

2015 in parliament even at the end of the year under review.

Financial Statement

NOTES TO ACCOUNTS

1. Notes to accounts

These accounting statements have been presented in compliance with generally accepted accounting principles and
by selecting the Sri Lanka public sector accounting policies endorsed by the public sector accounting standards com-
mittee, preparing accounting estimates in timely and fair manner.

It is assured that measures have been taken to present fair financial statements by designing implementing and main-
taining internal control relevant to the preparation and fair presentation of financial statements that are free from
material misstatement, whether due to fraud or error.

2. Accounting Policies

The accounting reports of the Authority have been presented with mutual interconnection between periods of time
and on historic cost basis in accordance with recognized accounting policies. Adjustments have been made towards
inflationary factors that may affect the financial policies and the accounting reports have been prepared on accrual

basis.

3. Location of the Authority

The Condominium Management Authority is located at the National Housing Development Authority at Sir Chittam-
palam A Gardianer Mawatha, Colombo 02 and carries out regulatory duties in respect of condominium properties
Covering the entire island.

a. Legal nature of the Authority

In terms of the powers conferred under the Common Amenities Board (Amendment) Act No. 24 of 2003, itis the
responsibility of the Authority to establish management corporations for the maintenance administration and control
of common elements and common amenities in condominium properties and to ensure that common facilities are
provided so as to fulfill the needs of stakeholders.

5. Legislation relevant for the administration of operations of the Authority
e Common Amenities Board (Amendment) Law No.l0 of 1073
° Common Amenities Board Act No. 46 of 1082
e Common Amenities Board (Amendment) Act No 24 of 2003
e Apartment Ownership Act No. 11 of 1073
e Apartment Ownership (Amendment) Act No. 45 of 1982
e Apartment Ownership {Special Provisions) No.04 19000
e Apartment Ownership (Amendment) Act 39 of 2003
6. Fixed assets

The provisions for depreciation for fixed assets are calculated by using straight line basis from the date of purchase to
the date of sale as per the policy of the Authority

e      Motor vehicles                                  -25% on Cost
e      Office furniture                                 -20% on cost
e      Machinery and equipment                 - 20% on cost
e      Office equipment                              - 20% on cost
e      Buildings                                       - 04% on cost

62


Financial Statement

07. Gratuity

Provisions have been made in the accounts on the basis of the period of service of all employees serving inthe
Authority for their gratuity. That value relevant to the year ended 31 December 2017 was Rs. 30,919,215 and it had
been invested as fixed deposits as at 31 December 2017.

058. Stocks

Adjustments have been made in the accounts having computed on the lesser value of the stocks purchase cost and
the net realized value and no profit percentage had been included.

9. Revenue
Profit/loss accounts have been prepared on the basis of gross revenue.
10. Allocations for bad and doubtrul debt

Allocations for bad and doubtful debt have been made on outcome on the basis of the age analysis of the debtors
existing as at the end of the year.

e      Years 0-2         10% 656,085

e      Years 2-3         20% 1,238,140
Ul)      Years 3-4         30%     64,470

e       Years 4-5           50% 3,630,382

Ul)      Over 5years 100% 6,930,200
Accordingly, a sum of Rs. 8,519,286 has been allocated in the accounts of the current year for bad and doubtful debt.
11. Contingent liabilities

A case has been filed in the district court of Colombo under case number 53429/MR to recover Rs 807,187 due from
Lanka Net (Pvt) Ltd. As there no contingent liabilities in respect of cases filed by or against the Authority, no allocations
have been made in the accounts for that purpose.

12. Lease loan

The said lease loan had been paid off by June 2017.

13. EPF and ETF in arrears

EPF 7 ETF contributions are paid for the employees of the Authority in terms of the provisions of the Employees
Provident Fund Act and as at 31.12.2017, there had not been any payable arrears.

14. Capital projects

Of Rs. 80,000,000 granted for the renovation of housing schemes in the year 2015, action had been taken to return Rs.
32,659,484 to the Ministry on 16th May 2017. Further, out of the money allocated in the year 2015 for the renovation
of roads of 03 housing schemes, Rs. 2,421,000 had been allocated for the remaining work relating to the granting of
title deeds of residents of Tsunami housing schemes. In addition, a Treasury provision amounting to Rs. 10,000,000 was
granted for conducting condominium awareness programmes in the year 2017 and of this amount Rs. 2,309,950 was
Spent on purchasing fixed items and Rs. 5,488,585 was deployed in the year 2017 on awareness programmes. Action
had been taken to use the balance of Rs. 2,201,464 in January 2018.



Financial Statement

15. Reserves

Revaluation reserves - Rs. 22,308,765

General reserves        - Rs. 1,350,000
Capital reserves         - Rs. 2,262,663
Total reserves            - Rs. 25,921,428

The above reserves to the value of Rs 25,92 1,42§ include Rs. 22,308,765 from the revaluation of fixed assets in the year
2008 and a capital transfer of Rs. 2,262,663.28 carried forward to the accounts of this Authority from its predecessor,

the Common Amenities Board.

16. Bonus shares

In pursuance of approval referred to by Ministry of Public Administration, Housing and Construction dated 12.01.1984,
5000 shares of Rs 100 were obtained from the Housing Development Finance Corporation on 19.01.1984.

A bonus share issue of 25,000 shares in respect of the value of the said shares was issued on 29.06.2000. Accordingly,
action has been taken to disclose in the accounts an investment of Rs. 3,000,000 for 30,000 shares of Rs. 100 each of
the HDFC in possession of this Authority.

17. Income Tax

Provisions have been allocated in accounts for the payment of Rs. 25,990,927 as income tax on the basis of the profit
of Rs. 124,375,570 for the said year as at 31.12.2017.

18. Accounting government grants

Inthe year 2017 too, the Treasury hadallocated Rs. 10,000,000 for creating awareness amongst partners of condominium
properties under the ‘Nagamu Purawara’ project and of that amount Rs. 7,798,535 had been spent inthe current year.
Similarly, action had been taken to include a sum of Rs 119,081 for the depreciation of fixed assets purchased for the
Said project in the project expenditure.

19. Allocation for depreciation

Action had been taken to depreciate fixed assets on the basis of percentages given in fixed assets note number 09.
Accordingly, action had been taken to adjust Rs. 7,984,344 as annual depreciation value to the profit of the current
year.
